Zakat — Almsgiving

Definition and Conditions of Sa'imah for Zakat
Defining the term sa'imah and its conditions for zakat obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sa'imah and identify the three conditions that make livestock zakatable according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Zakat on livestock requires the animals to be sa'imah: grazing most of the year and intended for breeding/dairy.

The term 'sa'imah' (grazing livestock) is a key technical term in Hanafi zakat law. Not all livestock are zakatable; only those that meet the specific definition of sa'imah. This lesson unpacks the definition and its conditions, showing how nuanced rulings can be derived from a single term.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the literal definition
The text defines sa'imah as 'that which suffices itself with grazing for most of the year.' Identify the key components: the animal depends on grazing, not stall-feeding, and this condition must hold for most of the year (more than half).
2
Understand the purpose condition
The commentary clarifies that the grazing must be intended for milk, offspring, or fattening. If the animal is used for work, riding, or meat, it is not sa'imah and no zakat is due.
This distinguishes productive assets from consumption assets.
3
Apply the temporal condition
The text specifies 'most of the year' – more than six months. If an animal is fed at home for half the year or more, it loses the status of sa'imah. The scholars also discuss what constitutes 'little fodder' that does not negate the status.
Half is the dividing line; the rulings are based on doubt (shakk) in the presence of the cause (sabab).
4
Distinguish grazing from stall-feeding
The passage covers the linguistics of 'ra'y' (grazing) and 'kala'' (herbage). A key point: if you bring herbage to the animal at home, it is not sa'imah. The animal must actively go out to graze.
This shows how terminology affects fiqh boundaries.
5
Apply the definition to classify livestock
Use the definition and conditions to determine whether a given herd is zakatable. Consider: feeding method, purpose, and duration of grazing.
This step consolidates the lesson's learning into practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة زكاة الأموال
والسائمة : هي المكتفية بالرّعى في أكثر الحول.
والسائمة : هي المكتفية بالرعي في أكثر الحول) الرعي بالكسر الكلا. قوله : هي المكتفية ؛ أي لقصدِ الدّرّ والنسل، ذكره في «التبيين)، وزاد في «المحيط»: والزيادة والسمن ليعم الذكور فقط.
وفي «البدائع»: «نصابُ السَّائمةِ له صفات منها : كونه معداً للإسامة للدر والنَّسل لما ذكرنا أنَّ مالَ الزَّكاة هو النامي، والمالُ النامي في الحيوان بالإسامة ؛ إذ به يحصل النسل فيزدادُ المال، فإن أسيمت للحمل والركوب أو اللحم فلا زكاة فيها". قوله : بالرعي ؛ هو بالفتح مصدر ، وبكسر الرَّاءِ نفس الكلا، واختار الشارح الثاني، وقال في «البحر» : المناسب هو الأول ، إذ لو حمل الكلأ إليها في البيت لا تكون سائمة. قوله : في أكثر الحول ؛ فلو علقها نصفه لا تكون سائمة، فلا زكاة فيها للشك في الموجب. كذا في «الدر المختار». وفي «فتح القدير»: «العَلَفُ اليسيرُ لا يزولُ به اسم الإسامة المستلزم للحكم ، وإذا كان مقابله كثيراً بالنسبة كان هو يسيراً، والنصفُ بالنسبة إلى النصف ليس كثيرا. قوله : الكلأ ؛ بفتح الكاف واللام ، بعدها همزة : العشب رطبه ويابسه. كذا في «القاموس» ، وفي «المغرب»: «الكلا: هو كلُّ ما رعته الدواب من الرطب واليابس
The Book of Zakat: Zakat on Wealth. And as-sa'imah: it is that which suffices itself with grazing for most of the year. (And as-sa'imah: it is that which suffices itself with grazing for most of the year) Grazing (ar-ra'y) broken ra' means herbage. His saying: 'it is that which suffices' i.e. for the purpose of milk and offspring, mentioned in at-Tabyin, and added in al-Muhit: 'and increase and fatness to include males only.' And in al-Bada'i': 'The nisab of sa'imah has conditions including: it is prepared for pasturing for milk and offspring because, as we mentioned, zakatable wealth is that which increases, and increase in animals is by pasturing; for through it offspring are obtained and wealth increases. So if it is pastured for carrying loads or riding or meat, then no zakat is due on it.' His saying: 'by grazing': the ra' with fatha is a verbal noun, and with kasra is the herbage itself, and the commentator chose the second, and said in al-Bahr: 'the appropriate is the first, because if one brings herbage to it at home, it would not be sa'imah.' His saying: 'for most of the year': so if it is contained for half of it, it is not sa'imah, so no zakat is due on it due to doubt in the cause. Similarly in ad-Durr al-Mukhtar. And in Fath al-Qadir: 'A little fodder does not remove the name of sa'imah which necessitates the ruling, and if its opposite is much in proportion, then it is little, and half in relation to half is not much.' His saying: 'al-kala' with fatha of kaf and lam followed by hamza: fresh and dry grass. Similarly in al-Qamus, and in al-Mughrib: 'Al-kala is everything that animals graze of fresh and dry.'
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'sa'imah' (grazing livestock) which is critical for zakat obligation on livestock. The author clarifies that sa'imah refers to livestock that depends on grazing for most of the year. The commentary expands: the grazing must be for the purpose of milk, offspring, or fattening—not for work or meat—otherwise no zakat. The amount of grazing: it must be for more than half the year; if confined and fed at home even for half the year, it is not sa'imah. The definition of 'ra'y' (grazing) is discussed: whether it means the act of grazing or the herbage itself. Also 'kala'' is defined as fresh/dry grass. All these nuances are from Hanafi sources like al-Tabyin, al-Muhit, al-Bada'i', al-Durr al-Mukhtar, Fath al-Qadir, etc.

Key Terms
السائمة (as-sa'imah): Livestock that grazes for most of the year, dependent on pasture, not stall-fed.
الرعي (ar-ra'y): The act of grazing or the herbage itself; context determines meaning.
الكلأ (al-kala'): Fresh and dry grass that animals graze.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which condition makes livestock liable for zakat as sa'imah?
A) The animal is used for carrying loads.
B) The animal grazes for more than half the year and is intended for breeding or dairy.
C) The animal is fed at home for the entire year.
D) The animal is used for riding.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of sa'imah is precise: livestock must graze for most of the year and be intended for breeding/dairy to be zakatable.

Rebel Takeover of Zakat: The General Framework
General framework and ruling for visible wealth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hidden and visible wealth for zakat purposes and state the Hanafi fatwa for visible wealth taken by rebels.

Core Idea
Zakat taken by rebels must be repeated secretly if misused, except land tax.

When rebels (bughah) take control of a town and collect zakat, the Hanafi school provides specific guidance. The first step is to understand the two categories of wealth: hidden (currency and trade goods not seen by the collector) and visible (livestock, crops, and what passes by the collector). This lesson outlines the general framework and the ruling for visible wealth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two wealth categories
From the text, hidden wealth (al-amwal al-batina) includes currency and trade goods not seen by the collector. Visible wealth (al-amwal al-zahira) includes livestock, crops, and items that pass by the collector.
2
Define the rebels (bughat)
Bughat are Muslims who rebel against the legitimate Imam. They are not kafir but their rule is illegitimate.
3
Apply the fatwa for visible wealth
If rebels take zakat on visible wealth, the owners are fatwaed to repeat the payment secretly if the rebels did not spend it in its rightful channels. This ensures the zakat reaches the proper recipients.
4
Note the exception for kharaj
Land tax (kharaj) is exempt from repetition. It is a government levy with no specified recipients, so its seizure by rebels is not subject to the same rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَخَذَ البغاة زكاة السوائم، والعشر، والخراج ، يُفتى أن يعيدوا خُفْيَةً إِن لم تُصْرَفْ في حقه لا الخراج. (أَخَذَ البغاة زكاة السوائم ، والعشر، والخراج ، يُفتى أن يعيدوا خُفية إن لم تُصْرَفْ فِي حَقِّهِ لا الخراج). اعلم أن ولاية أخذِ الخراج للإمام ، وكذا أخذ الزَّكاة في الأموال الظاهرة، وهي : عشر الخارج، وزكاة السوائم ، وزكاة أموال التجارة. قوله : البغاة ، بالضم : جمع الباغي، وهم قوم مسلمون خرجوا عن طاعة الإمام الحق، فإذا ظهروا وغلبوا على بلدة وأخذوا الزكاة من أرباب الأموال، فإن كانت زكاة الأموال الباطنة : وهي النقود وعروض التجارة إذا لم يمر بها على العاشر، فاختلف في الأجزاء بالأداء إليهم : ففي «الولوالجية»: المفتى به عدم الإجزاء. وفي «المبسوط»: الصحة إذا نوى بالدفع لظلمة زماننا الصدقة عليهم ؛ لأنهم بما عليهم من التَّبعاتِ فقراء. وإن كانت زكاة الأموال الظاهرة : وهي السَّوائمُ وما فيه، والعشر والخراج وما يمر به على العاشر، وسيأتي تفصيلُ هذه الثلاثة في مواضعها إن شاء الله، فقيل: يجزئ الأداء إليهم ، وقيل : يفتى للملاكِ أن يعيدوا زكاة أموالهم ويصرفُوها في مصارفها إن لم تصرفه البغاة في حقها. قوله : خفية ، بالضم : أي سراً ، واختفاء، فإنه لو أعلن لأخذوا به ثانياً.
The rebels took the zakat of grazing livestock, the tithe, and the land tax; it is fatwaed that they should repeat it secretly if it was not spent in its due place, except the land tax. (The rebels took the zakat of grazing livestock, the tithe, and the land tax; it is fatwaed that they should repeat it secretly if it was not spent in its due place, except the land tax.) Know that the authority to take the land tax belongs to the Imam, and likewise the taking of zakat on visible wealth, which is: tithe of produce, zakat of grazing livestock, and zakat of trade goods. His saying: 'al-bughat' with damma: plural of al-baghi, and they are a group of Muslims who rebelled against the authority of the righteous Imam. So if they appear and overcome a town and take zakat from the owners of wealth, then if it is zakat of hidden wealth: which is currency and trade goods that have not passed by the collector (al-'ashir), then there is disagreement on the validity of payment to them: In al-Walwalijiyyah: the fatwa is that it is not valid. In al-Mabsut: validity if one intends by paying, due to the oppressors of our time, charity to them because they are poor due to the debts upon them. And if it is zakat of visible wealth: which is grazing livestock and what is in it, and the tithe and land tax and what passes by the collector, and the detail of these three will come in their places in shaa Allah. So it is said: payment to them is valid, and it is said: the fatwa for the owners is that they should repeat the zakat of their wealth and distribute it in its proper channels if the rebels did not spend it in its due place. His saying: 'secretly' with damma: i.e., covertly and hidden, for if they announce it, they would take it a second time.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage deals with a practical problem: when rebels (bughah) take control of a town and collect zakat. The Hanafi ruling differentiates between hidden wealth (like cash and trade goods not seen by the collector) and visible wealth (like livestock and crops). For hidden wealth, there is a difference: according to al-Walwalijiyyah, paying to rebels is not valid; according to al-Mabsut, it is valid if the payer intends it as charity to the rebels because they are considered poor due to their situation. However, for visible wealth, the fatwa recommends that the owners should repeat the zakat secretly if the rebels did not spend it in its proper place. The exception is the land tax (kharaj), which is not to be repeated because it is a government levy. The term 'bughat' is defined as Muslims who rebel against the legitimate Imam.

Key Terms
البغاة (al-bughat): Muslims who rebel against the legitimate Imam.
الخراج (al-kharaj): Land tax levied on agricultural land by the Imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the exception to the rule that owners should repeat zakat if rebels took it?
A) Zakat on grazing livestock.
B) The tithe (ushr).
C) The land tax (kharaj).
D) Zakat on trade goods.

Key Takeaway
Visible wealth zakat taken by rebels must be repeated secretly if misused, but land tax is exempt.

Hidden Wealth: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hidden wealth zakat to rebels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on paying zakat on hidden wealth to rebels and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Paying hidden wealth zakat to rebels is disputed: some say it fails to discharge; others allow it as charity due to rebels' poverty.

For hidden wealth (currency and trade goods not seen by the collector), Hanafi scholars disagree on whether paying zakat to rebels suffices. Al-Walwalijiyyah holds it is invalid, while al-Mabsut permits it if intended as charity. This lesson explores the arguments and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of dispute
The dispute concerns zakat on hidden wealth (al-amwal al-batina) when taken by rebels.
2
State the first position (al-Walwalijiyyah)
According to al-Walwalijiyyah, payment of hidden wealth zakat to rebels is not valid and does not discharge the obligation. The owner must pay again to the rightful recipients.
3
State the second position (al-Mabsut)
Al-Mabsut holds that payment is valid if the owner intended it as charity to the rebels, because the rebels are considered poor due to their debts.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a Muslim pays hidden wealth zakat to rebels and follows al-Mabsut, he is discharged; if he follows al-Walwalijiyyah, he must repeat the payment.
5
Note the tarjih
The text suggests the fatwa in al-Walwalijiyyah (non-validity) is more adhered to, but the dispute remains active.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(أَخَذَ البغاة زكاة السوائم ، والعشر، والخراج ، يُفتى أن يعيدوا خُفية إن لم تُصْرَفْ فِي حَقِّهِ لا الخراج). اعلم أن ولاية أخذِ الخراج للإمام ، وكذا أخذ الزَّكاة في الأموال الظاهرة، وهي : عشر الخارج، وزكاة السوائم ، وزكاة أموال التجارة. قوله : البغاة ، بالضم : جمع الباغي، وهم قوم مسلمون خرجوا عن طاعة الإمام الحق، فإذا ظهروا وغلبوا على بلدة وأخذوا الزكاة من أرباب الأموال، فإن كانت زكاة الأموال الباطنة : وهي النقود وعروض التجارة إذا لم يمر بها على العاشر، فاختلف في الأجزاء بالأداء إليهم : ففي «الولوالجية»: المفتى به عدم الإجزاء. وفي «المبسوط»: الصحة إذا نوى بالدفع لظلمة زماننا الصدقة عليهم ؛ لأنهم بما عليهم من التَّبعاتِ فقراء. وإن كانت زكاة الأموال الظاهرة : وهي السَّوائمُ وما فيه، والعشر والخراج وما يمر به على العاشر، وسيأتي تفصيلُ هذه الثلاثة في مواضعها إن شاء الله، فقيل: يجزئ الأداء إليهم ، وقيل : يفتى للملاكِ أن يعيدوا زكاة أموالهم ويصرفُوها في مصارفها إن لم تصرفه البغاة في حقها. قوله : خفية ، بالضم : أي سراً ، واختفاء، فإنه لو أعلن لأخذوا به ثانياً.

Ruling on Rebels Taking Zakat, 'Ushr, and Kharaj
Expansion of the ruling on rebels' collection of obligatory wealth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether owners must repeat zakat, 'ushr, and kharaj when taken by rebels, distinguishing between hidden and apparent wealth, and identify the condition that triggers repetition.

Core Idea
Payment to rebels discharges zakat only if spent correctly; kharaj always suffices.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah addresses a practical scenario of rebellion: when insurgent forces seize obligatory wealth from Muslims. The Hanafi school distinguishes between different types of wealth and whether the rebels spent it on the rightful recipients. Understanding this ruling protects a Muslim from double liability while ensuring the poor do not lose their due.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wealth type
Determine whether the seized wealth is hidden (batinah: cash, trade goods not passing 'ashir) or apparent (zahirah: livestock, 'ushr, kharaj, goods passing 'ashir). This classification affects the ruling.
Hidden wealth is not subject to the Imam's collection in the standard view.
2
Examine the rebels' disbursement
If the rebels spent the wealth on the eight categories of zakat mentioned in Quran 9:60, the owner's obligation is fulfilled. If they misspent, repetition is required.
For apparent wealth (zakat and 'ushr), the fatwa is to repeat if misspent.
3
Apply the kharaj exception
Kharaj is never required to be repeated, because its legitimate recipients are the fighters (muqatilah). Since rebels fight disbelievers, they fall into that category.
This exception is based on the purpose of kharaj: military expenditure.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on hidden wealth
According to al-Walwalijiyyah (mufta bihi), hidden zakat paid to rebels does not suffice; the owner must repeat. According to al-Mabsut (Imam Muhammad), it suffices if the owner intended charity to the rebels.
The mufta bihi follows the choice of Abu Bakr al-A'mash, supported by major Hanafi texts.
5
Implement the fatwa secretly
If repetition is required, it must be done secretly (khufyatan) to avoid the rebels taking it again.
Open repetition would lead to double seizure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَخَذَ البغاة زكاة السوائم، والعشر، والخراج ، يُفتى أن يعيدوا خُفْيَةً إِن لم تُصْرَفْ في حقه لا الخراج.

اعلم أن ولاية أخذِ الخراج للإمام ، وكذا أخذ الزَّكاة في الأموال الظاهرة، وهي : عشر الخارج، وزكاة السوائم ، وزكاة أموال التجارة
[١] قوله : البغاة ، بالضم : جمع الباغي، وهم قوم مسلمون خرجوا عن طاعة الإمام الحق، فإذا ظهروا وغلبوا على بلدة وأخذوا الزكاة من أرباب الأموال، فإن كانت زكاة الأموال الباطنة : وهي النقود وعروض التجارة إذا لم يمر بها على العاشر، فاختلف في الأجزاء بالأداء إليهم :
ففي «الولوالجية»: المفتى به عدم الإجزاء.
وفي «المبسوط»: الصحة إذا نوى بالدفع لظلمة زماننا الصدقة عليهم ؛ لأنهم بما عليهم من التَّبعاتِ فقراء. وإن كانت زكاة الأموال الظاهرة : وهي السَّوائمُ وما فيه، والعشر والخراج وما يمر به على العاشر، وسيأتي تفصيلُ هذه الثلاثة في مواضعها إن شاء الله، فقيل: يجزئ الأداء إليهم ، وقيل : يفتى للملاكِ أن يعيدوا زكاة أموالهم ويصرفُوها في مصارفها إن لم تصرفه البغاة في حقها.
[٢]قوله : خفية ، بالضم : أي سراً ، واختفاء، فإنه لو أعلن لأخذوا به ثانياً.

(۱) البغاة: قوم من المسلمين خرجوا عن طاعة الإمام العدل بحيث يستحلون قتل العادل وماله بتأويل القرآن... ينظر : حاشية الشلبي على التبيين (۱) : (۲) ما ذكر المصنف ونصره الشارح فيه هو اختيار أبي بكر الأعمش وعليه مشت عامة الكتب ك(الهداية) (۱) : (۱۰۳) ، و(الملتقى (ص) (۳۰)، والتنوير) (۲) : (٢٤) ، و(الغرر» (۱ : ۱۸۰)، وغيرها.

فإن أخذ البغاة، أو سلاطين زماننا الخراج، فلا إعادة على الملاك ؛ لأنَّ مصرف الخراج المقاتلة"، وهم من المقاتلة ؛ لأنهم يُحاربون الكفار.
وإن أخذوا الزَّكاة المذكورة" المقدرة.
فإن صرفوا إلى مصارفها، وهي : مصارفُ الزَّكاة، فلا إعادة على الملاك.
[٦] وإن لم يصرفوا الى مصارفها، فعليهم الإعادة خُفيةً

(۱) قوله : العاشر ؛ هو من ينصبه الإمام على الطريق لأخذ زكاة التجارة والعشر ونحوها، قال في «المحيط»: إن للإمام أخذ الزَّكاة في روايةٍ بسبب الحماية حتى اختص الأخذ بمثل السوائم وأموال التجارة التي تكون في المفاوز لا في الأموال الباطنة التي تكون في البلدان ؛ لأنها لا تكون محمية بحماية الإمام. وفي رواية : لا بسبب الحماية، بل لأجل الولاية الثابتة له شرعاً ، كان له أخذ زكاة الأموال الباطنة أيضاً ، لكن قد انقطعت ولايته بسبب غلبة الخوارج.
[٢]قوله : المقاتلة ؛ على صيغة اسم فاعل : أي الذين يقاتلون الكفار فيصرفُ الخراج في تجهيزهم واهتمامهم.
[٣] قوله : الزكاة المذكورة ؛ أي زكاةُ السَّوائم، والعشر، وزكاة أموال التجارة.
[٤] قوله : وهي مصارفُ الزَّكاة ؛ المذكورة في قوله : إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَتُ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَالْمَسَكِينِ (۲) الآية ، وسيأتي ذكرها في موضعها.
[0]قوله : فلا إعادة ؛ أي لا يجب عليهم أداؤها مرة ثانية لحصول المقصودِ من الأداء وهو كونه مصروفاً إلى المصارف.
[٦] قوله : فعليهم ؛ أي على الملاكِ أن يؤدُّوها ثانياً.

(1) العاشر: هو من نصبه الإمام على الطريق ؛ لأخذ صدقة التجار؛ ليأمنوا من اللصوص، ويشترط أن يكون حراً مسلماً غير هاشمي. ينظر : «درر الحکام»(۱ : ۱۸۲) الشرنبلالي عليه.
حاشية
(٢) التوبة : من الآية ٦٠ وتمامها : وَالْعَمِلِينَ عَلَيْهَا وَالْمُؤَلَّفَةِ قُلُوبُهُمْ وَفِي الرِّقَابِ وَالْغَرِمِينَ وَفِي سَبِيلِ اللهِ وَابْنِ السَّبِيلِ فَرِيضَةً مِنَ اللهِ وَاللهُ عَلِيمٌ حَكِيرٌ .
The rebels took the zakat of grazing animals, and the 'ushr, and the kharaj. It is given as a fatwa that they should repeat (the payment) secretly if it is not spent in its rightful place, except for the kharaj.

Know that the authority to take kharaj belongs to the Imam, and similarly the taking of zakat on apparent wealth, which is: the 'ushr of the produce, and the zakat of grazing animals, and the zakat of trade goods.
[1] His saying: al-bughah, with damm: plural of baghi, and they are a group of Muslims who have disobeyed the just Imam. So when they appear and overcome a town and take zakat from the owners of wealth, if it is zakat of hidden wealth: which is cash and trade goods that have not passed by the 'ashir, then there is a difference of opinion regarding its sufficiency by paying to them: In al-Walwalijiyyah: the fatwa is that it does not suffice. In al-Mabsut: it is valid if one intends by paying, due to the oppressors of our time, charity to them, because they are poor due to the liabilities upon them. And if it is zakat of apparent wealth: which is grazing animals and what is in them, and 'ushr and kharaj and what passes by the 'ashir, and the detail of these three will come in their places, insha'Allah. It is said: payment to them suffices, and it is said: a fatwa is given to the owners that they should repeat the zakat of their wealth and spend it in its categories if the rebels did not spend it in its rightful place.
[2] His saying: khufyatan, with damm: i.e., secretly, and concealment, for if he announces, they would take it again.

(1) al-bughah: a group of Muslims who have disobeyed the just Imam such that they consider it lawful to kill the just person and take his property based on a misinterpretation of the Qur'an... see Hashiyat al-Shalabi 'ala al-Tabyin (1): (2) What the author mentioned and the commentator supported is the choice of Abu Bakr al-A'mash and upon it go the general books like al-Hidayah (1): (103), al-Multaqa (p. 30), al-Tanwir (2): (24), al-Ghurar (1:180), and others.

If the rebels, or the sultans of our time, take the kharaj, then there is no repetition upon the owners, because the recipients of kharaj are the fighters, and they are among the fighters because they fight the disbelievers. And if they take the aforementioned zakat in the estimated amount, and they spend it in its categories, which are the categories of zakat, then there is no repetition upon the owners. [6] And if they do not spend it in its categories, then they must repeat it secretly.

(1) His saying: al-'ashir; he is the one whom the Imam appoints on the road to take zakat of trade and 'ushr and similar. He said in al-Muhit: The Imam has the right to take zakat in one narration due to protection, so the taking is specific to grazing animals and trade goods that are in deserts, not hidden wealth that is in towns, because they are not protected by the protection of the Imam. In another narration: not due to protection, but for the sake of the authority established for him by Shari'ah, he may also take zakat on hidden wealth, but his authority has been cut off due to the dominance of the khawarij.
[2] His saying: al-muqatilah; on the pattern of active participle: i.e., those who fight the disbelievers, so kharaj is spent on equipping and caring for them.
[3] His saying: the aforementioned zakat; i.e., zakat of grazing animals, 'ushr, and zakat of trade goods.
[4] His saying: and they are the categories of zakat; mentioned in His saying: Indeed the charities are for the poor and the needy (2) the verse, and it will be mentioned in its place.
[0] His saying: no repetition; i.e., they are not obligated to perform it a second time because the purpose of payment has been achieved, which is being spent in its categories.
[6] His saying: upon them; i.e., upon the owners they must perform it a second time.

(1) al-'ashir: he is the one appointed by the Imam on the road to take charity from merchants so that they are safe from thieves, and it is required that he be free, Muslim, and non-Hashimi. See Durar al-Hukkam (1:182) with the hashiya of al-Shurunbulali.
Hashiyah
(2) al-Tawbah: from verse 60, and its full text: and the workers upon it, and those whose hearts are reconciled, and for freeing captives, and for debtors, and in the way of Allah, and for the traveler, an obligation from Allah, and Allah is Knowing, Wise.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is an expansion (sharh) on the ruling of rebels (bughah) who forcibly take zakat, 'ushr, and kharaj. The commentator begins by restating the matn: rebels taking zakat of grazing livestock (sawa'im), 'ushr (a tithe on crops and trade), and kharaj (land tax) triggers a fatwa that the owners must secretly repeat payment if the rebels did not spend it in its rightful channels, except for kharaj (no repeat needed).

The commentator first clarifies the types of wealth. He distinguishes between 'hidden wealth' (amwal al-batinah: cash and trade goods not passing by the 'ashir) and 'apparent wealth' (amwal al-zahirah: grazing livestock, 'ushr, kharaj, and goods that do pass by the 'ashir). For hidden wealth paid to rebels, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the fatwa in al-Walwalijiyyah says it does not suffice (must be paid again), while al-Mabsut holds it suffices if the payer intended it as charity for the rebels, considering them poor due to their burdens. For apparent wealth, some say payment to rebels suffices, but the preferred fatwa is that owners must repeat the payment secretly if the rebels did not spend it correctly.

When it comes to kharaj, the commentator rules that no repetition is required, because the recipient of kharaj are the fighters (muqatilah) who fight disbelievers. Since rebels fight disbelievers, they fall into that category, so the payment reaches its rightful consumers. Similarly, if rebels take the zakat and actually spend it on the eight categories mentioned in Surah al-Tawbah (9:60), the owners are not required to repeat. However, if they take it but spend it elsewhere, the owners must secretly repeat the payment to avoid being collected again.

The commentary also includes important definitions: 'bughah' are Muslims who rebel against the just Imam, justifying killing and taking property based on misinterpretation. 'Al-'ashir' is the official appointed to collect zakat on roads. 'Al-muqatilah' are those who fight disbelievers. The Hanafi position here is the choice of Abu Bakr al-A'mash, supported by many authoritative texts like al-Hidayah, al-Multaqa, and al-Tanwir. The underlying evidence includes the Quranic verse on zakat categories and the principle that kharaj is for military expenses.

Key Terms
البغاة (al-bughah): A group of Muslims who revolt against the just Imam, considering it lawful to kill him and take his property based on a misinterpretation of the Qur’an.
العاشر (al-'āshir): The official appointed by the Imam on roads to collect zakat on trade goods and 'ushr.
المقاتلة (al-muqātilah): The fighters who engage in jihad against disbelievers; the recipients of kharaj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi fatwa in this passage, when must the owners of livestock secretly repeat their zakat payment after rebels have taken it?
A) Always, regardless of what rebels do with it.
B) Only if the rebels did not spend the zakat in its proper categories.
C) Only if the rebels spent the zakat on the poor.
D) Never, because payment to rebels always suffices.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school protects the rights of the poor by requiring repetition of zakat and 'ushr if rebels misappropriate them, but exempts kharaj because it reaches its intended recipients (fighters) even through rebels.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
7 min
Ruling on Zakat Taken by Rebels or Unjust Rulers
Explains when zakat must be repeated if taken by rebels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether zakat must be repeated when taken by rebels, and distinguish between kharaj and zakat in this context.

Core Idea
Rebel-taken zakat must be repeated secretly if not spent on the eight categories.

This lesson examines a nuanced situation: when rebels or unjust rulers forcibly collect zakat or kharaj from Muslims. Does this payment fulfill the obligation? The Hanafi school analyzes two separate categories—kharaj spent on combatants and zakat spent on its eight recipients—and provides a detailed ruling that balances practical necessity with religious duty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of payments
The passage distinguishes between kharaj (land tax) and zakat. Kharaj is spent on combatants, while zakat has specific eight categories of recipients.
The ruling for each differs based on the intended expenditure.
2
Understand the ruling for kharaj
If rebels take kharaj, there is no repetition on the owners because the rebels are considered combatants (muqatila) who fight against non-Muslims, so the kharaj reaches its proper recipients.
This is unconditional; no need to check how rebels spend it.
3
Understand the conditional ruling for zakat
If rebels take zakat, the obligation is only fulfilled if they actually spend it on the eight categories mentioned in Quran 9:60. If they do, no repetition. If they do not, the owner must pay zakat again secretly.
The condition is whether the zakat reached the correct recipients.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Three opinions exist: (1) no repetition regardless; (2) zakat falls by intention; (3) repetition if not spent correctly (chosen view). The first two are considered weak.
The chosen view is that of Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah.
5
Understand the practical consequence
The repetition is wajib diyaanatan (a religious duty between the person and God), not enforceable by court due to rebel domination. The payment must be made secretly to avoid further oppression.
This is a precautionary measure (ihtiyat).

كتاب الزكاة زكاة الأموال ما دامت تحت حماية العاشر فإن أخذ البغاة، أو سلاطين زماننا الخراج، فلا إعادة على الملاك ؛ لأنَّ مصرف الخراج المقاتلة، وهم من المقاتلة ؛ لأنهم يُحاربون الكفار. وإن أخذوا الزَّكاة المذكورة المقدرة. فإن صرفوا إلى مصارفها، وهي : مصارفُ الزَّكاة، فلا إعادة على الملاك. (1) العاشر: هو من نصبه الإمام على الطريق ؛ لأخذ صدقة التجار؛ ليأمنوا من اللصوص، ويشترط أن يكون حراً مسلماً غير هاشمي. ينظر : «درر الحکام»(۱ : ۱۸۲) الشرنبلالي عليه. حاشية (٢) التوبة : من الآية ٦٠ وتمامها : وَالْعَمِلِينَ عَلَيْهَا وَالْمُؤَلَّفَةِ قُلُوبُهُمْ وَفِي الرِّقَابِ وَالْغَرِمِينَ وَفِي سَبِيلِ اللهِ وَابْنِ السَّبِيلِ فَرِيضَةً مِنَ اللهِ وَاللهُ عَلِيمٌ حَكِيرٌ . أي يؤدُّونَها إلى مستحقيها فيما بينهم وبين الله. وإنما قال : يُفتى أن يعيدوا خُفْيَةً ؛ احترازاً عن قول بعض المشايخ : إنَّه لا إعادة عليهم ؛ لأنهم لما تسلّطوا على المسلمين ، فحكمهم حكم الإمام ضرورة ؛ ولهذا يصح منهم تفويض القضاء، وإقامة الجمع والأعياد، ونحو ذلك. [١]قوله : إلى مستحقيها؛ بكسر الحاء المهملة : أي الذين يستحقون الزكاة وهم المسمون بالمصارف. [٢]قوله : فيما بينهم وبين الله؛ أي لا يعلمه إلا هو وربه من غير أن يطلع عليه السلطان أو نوابه؛ لئلا يؤدى ويُتَغَلَّب عليه. [۳] قوله : احترازاً ... الخ؛ الحاصلُ : أنّ في المسألة ثلاثة أقوال : أحدها: أنهم إذا أخذوا زكاة الأموال الظاهرة لا إعادة على المالك سواء علم صرفهم في المصارف أو لم يعلم. وثانيهما : أنه تسقط الزَّكاةُ بنيَّةِ التَّصدق عليهم، فلا حاجة إلى الإعادة، وهذان القولان ضعيفان، كما بسطَهُ الشَّارحُ له فيما يأتي عن قريب. وثالثهما : ما اختاره المصنف له أنهم يعيدونها خفية، وظاهر كلامه أنه واجب عليهم ديانة فيما بينه وبين الله ، وقيل : إن هذا الحكم احتياطاً. وعلى كل قول إذا غلب الإمام الحق لا يثنى عليهم بعدما أخذت البغاة زكاة أموالهم الظاهرة ؛ لأنَّ الإمام يحميهم. كذا في «الهداية). (٤) قوله : لأنهم لما تسلّطوا... الخ؛ حاصله : أنَّ البغاة لَمَّا غلبوا علينا، وحصل لهم التسلط قهراً ، فحكمهم حكم الإمام الحق، ومن ثم يصح منهم ما يصح من الإمام الحق؛ كتقرير القضاة في البلاد، والاهتمام بإقامة صلاة العيدين والجمعة وغير ذلك مما هو من شعائر الإسلام : أي أفعاله الظاهرة التي جعلت علامات عليه، فلما أخذوا زكاةً أموالنا صح منهم ذلك؛ لقيامهم مقامَ الإمام ولو عنوة ، فلا تجب إعادتها على الملاك. (۱) «الهداية» (۲ : ۱۹۹)
The Book of Zakat: Zakat on Wealth. As long as it is under the protection of the tithe collector. If rebels or the rulers of our time take the kharaj (land tax), there is no repetition upon the owners, because the expenditure of kharaj is for the combatants, and they (the rebels) are among the combatants because they fight the disbelievers. And if they take the aforementioned zakat that is fixed, then if they spend it on its recipients, which are the categories of zakat, there is no repetition upon the owners. [6] And if they do not spend it on its recipients, then upon them (the owners) is to repeat it secretly. (1) His statement: 'al-‘ashir': he is the one appointed by the Imam on the road to take zakat of trade and tithe and similar. He said in 'al-Muhit': The Imam has the right to take zakat in one narration due to protection, so the taking is specific to such as grazing livestock and trade goods that are in the wilderness, not the hidden wealth that is in the cities, because they are not protected by the Imam's protection. In another narration: not due to protection, but because of the authority established for him by Shari‘ah, he may take zakat of hidden wealth also, but his authority has been cut off due to the dominance of the Khawarij. [2] His statement: 'al-muqatilah': in the form of active participle: meaning those who fight the disbelievers, so the kharaj is spent on their equipment and affairs. [3] His statement: 'the aforementioned zakat': meaning zakat of grazing livestock, tithe, and zakat of trade goods. [4] His statement: 'which are the categories of zakat': mentioned in His statement: Indeed the charities are for the poor and the needy... verse, and its mention will come in its place. [0] His statement: 'there is no repetition': meaning it is not obligatory for them to pay it a second time, because the purpose of payment has been achieved, namely it being spent on the recipients. [6] His statement: 'upon them': meaning upon the owners to pay it a second time. (1) The 'ashir: he is the one appointed by the Imam on the road to take the charity of the merchants, to secure safety from thieves; it is required that he be free, Muslim, not a Hashimi. See 'Durar al-Hukkam' (1:182) with al-Shurunbulali's commentary. Footnote: (2) Surah al-Tawbah: part of verse 60, its completion: And the workers upon it, and those whose hearts are reconciled, and for the captives, and the debtors, and in the way of God, and the wayfarer, an obligation from God. And God is Knowing, Wise. Meaning they pay it to its recipients, between them and God. He only said: 'a fatwa that they repeat secretly' as a precaution against the statement of some scholars: that there is no repetition upon them, because when they (the rebels) overpower the Muslims, their judgment is the judgment of the Imam by necessity; hence the delegation of the judiciary, and the establishment of Friday prayers and Eid prayers, and similar matters are valid from them. [1] His statement: 'to its recipients': with the kasra on the important letter: meaning those who deserve zakat, and they are the ones called the categories. [2] His statement: 'between them and God': meaning no one knows it except him and his Lord, without the Sultan or his deputies being aware, lest he be subjected to them. [3] His statement: 'as a precaution... etc.': the conclusion is that in this matter there are three opinions: One: that if they take zakat of apparent wealth, there is no repetition on the owner, whether he knows they spent it on the recipients or not. Second: that the zakat falls by intending to give charity to them, so there is no need for repetition; these two opinions are weak, as the commentator has expanded on them shortly after. Third: what the author (of al-Hidayah) chose: that they repeat it secretly, and the apparent meaning of his statement is that it is obligatory upon them as a religious duty between him and God, and it is said that this is a precautionary measure. In any case, when the rightful Imam prevails, no repetition is required after the rebels took zakat of their apparent wealth, because the Imam protects them. As in 'al-Hidayah'. (4) His statement: 'because when they overpower... etc.': its conclusion is that since the rebels dominated us and achieved power by force, their judgment is the judgment of the rightful Imam; therefore, what is valid from the rightful Imam is valid from them, such as appointing judges in the land, and taking care of the performance of Eid al-Adha and Friday prayers, and other similar matters from the symbols of Islam: meaning the apparent actions that are made signs of it. So when they take zakat of our wealth, it is valid from them due to their standing in place of the Imam, even if by force, so repetition is not obligatory upon the owners. (1) 'al-Hidayah' (2:199).
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the text of Al-Wiqayah discussing the ruling on zakat and kharaj when taken by rebels or unjust rulers. It clarifies two separate categories: kharaj (land tax) and zakat. For kharaj taken by rebels, there is no need to repeat because the rebels are among the muqatila (combatants) who fight against non-Muslims, and the kharaj is spent on them, so the payment reaches the correct recipients. For zakat, the passage distinguishes based on whether the rebels actually spent the zakat on its prescribed eight categories (as per Surah Tawbah). If they did, then no repetition is required. If they did not, then the owners must pay again, but secretly (khufyatan) to avoid being subjected to the rebels. The commentary then explains the meaning of 'ashir (the tax collector appointed by the Imam), muqatila (combatants), and the different transmissions (riwayat) regarding the authority of the Imam to take zakat. It notes that in one narration, the Imam's authority is restricted to apparent wealth (like livestock and trade goods) due to his protection of the roads, while in another narration, his authority extends to hidden wealth as well, but this authority is cut off due to the dominance of the Khawarij (rebels). The passage also refutes the opinion of some scholars that since the rebels have usurped authority, their judgment is like that of the rightful Imam, so no repetition is needed. However, the chosen position (as per the author of Al-Hidayah) is that repetition is required if the funds were not spent correctly, and this repetition is to be done secretly. Three opinions are mentioned: (1) no repetition at all, (2) zakat is cancelled by intention, (3) the chosen one: repeat in secret. The first two are considered weak. The ruling is that it is wajib diyaanatan (a religious duty between the person and God), not enforceable by a court due to the circumstances. The text emphasizes that this is a precautionary measure. It also states that if the rightful Imam regains power, no repetition is needed because the Imam will protect the people.

Key Terms
العاشر (al-‘āshir): The tax collector appointed by the Imam to collect zakat on trade and tithe from merchants on the road.
المقاتلة (al-muqātilah): Those who fight the disbelievers, i.e., combatants; the kharaj is spent on their equipment and needs.
البغاة (al-bughāt): Rebels who oppose the rightful Imam and seize power by force.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen Hanafi position in this passage, when must the owner repeat zakat secretly?
A) When rebels take kharaj (land tax).
B) When rebels take zakat and spend it on the eight categories.
C) When rebels take zakat and do not spend it on the eight categories.
D) When the rightful Imam takes zakat.

Key Takeaway
Zakat taken by rebels requires secret repetition if not spent on the Quranically prescribed eight categories.

Repeating Zakat Taken by Rebels: Necessity Limited
Intra-Hanafi dispute on repetition of zakat taken by rebels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on repeating zakat taken by rebels and evaluate the opposing intra-madhhab argument using the principle of necessity.

Core Idea
Necessity is limited to its extent: rebels' acts are valid only where essential, not for zakat which can be paid secretly.

This lesson examines a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school: if rebels (bughāt) seize zakat from Muslims, must the owners repeat the payment? The discussion involves the principle of necessity, the distinction between diyānah and qadā', and the correct interpretation of Quranic verses on charity. By understanding this dispute, you will learn how Hanafi scholars apply the maxim 'necessities are restricted to their measure' and how they weigh different proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three opinions within the Hanafi school
List the three views mentioned in the passage: no repetition, repetition dropped by intention to give charity, and repetition secretly (the chosen view). Which is considered weak and why?
The author explicitly labels the first two weak.
2
Understand the opposing argument for no repetition
Some scholars (e.g., Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani) argue that rebels, by overpowering, act as the imam by necessity. Therefore, their taking zakat is valid and no repetition is needed.
This argument is based on the necessity to maintain public order.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response using the necessity principle
The response states that what is established by necessity is limited to its extent. Only essential functions like judges and prayers are permitted; taking zakat is not necessary because the owner can pay secretly.
The key principle: 'ما ثبت بالضرورة يتقدر بقدرها'.
4
Critique the claim that the original ruling for zakat is secrecy
The passage criticizes the idea that zakat is best paid secretly. It points out three contradictions: the ruler's authority over apparent wealth, the preference for openness in obligatory charity, and the Quranic verse referring to voluntary charity.
The verse 2:271 is interpreted to apply to voluntary sadaqah, not zakat.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view, as chosen by al-Sarakhsi in al-Mabsut, is that the owner must repeat the zakat secretly (diyanatan). This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
Al-Sarakhsi considers this the asahh (sounder) view.

(٤) قوله : لأنهم لما تسلّطوا... الخ ؛ حاصله : أنَّ البغاة لَمَّا غلبوا علينا، وحصل لهم التسلط قهراً ، فحكمهم حكم الإمام الحق، ومن ثم يصح منهم ما يصح من الإمام الحق ؛ كتقرير القضاة في البلاد، والاهتمام بإقامة صلاة العيدين والجمعة وغير ذلك مما هو من شعائر الإسلام : أي أفعاله الظاهرة التي جعلت علامات عليه، فلما أخذوا زكاةً أموالنا صح منهم ذلك ؛ لقيامهم مقامَ الإمام ولو عنوة ، فلا تجب إعادتها على الملاك. (٢) قوله : فإن الأصل فيه الأداء خفية ؛ فيه بحث من وجوه : أحدها: أنه مخالف لتصريحاتهم بأن ولاية أخذ الزكاة في الأموال الظاهرة للسلطان، فإنه لو كان الأصل والأفضل في أداءِ الزَّكاة الاختفاء لما كان الأمر كذلك. وثانيها : أنه مخالف لتصريحاتهم أنَّ الأفضل في الصدقات الواجبة ومنها الزَّكاةُ الإعلان، وفضلُ الإخفاء إنّما هو في صدقاتِ التَّطوع، كما في «خزانة المفتين» وغيره ، وإنما كانت المجاهرةُ بالزَّكاةِ أفضلُ لنفي التهمة. وثالثها : أنَّ الآية التي استدل بها على كون الأصل في الزَّكاةِ الخفية محمولة على صدقات التطوع، صرح به في «الكشاف»، وغيره ، فلا يتم التقريب، ويؤيده أنَّ النبي كان يبعث عمالاً إلى أصحاب الأموال لأخذِ الزَّكاةِ كما لا يخفى على من طالع كتب الحديث، وبالجملة فذكر هذا الأصلُ غير صحيح، ولا حاجة إليه، فإن المقصود يتم بدونه كما أشرنا إليه. (۱) البقرة ، (۲۷۱) ، وتمامها : إن تُبْدُوا الصَّدَقَاتِ فَنِعِمَّا هِيَ وَإِن تُخْفُوهَا وَتُؤْتُوهَا الْفُقَرَاءَ فَهُوَ خَيْرٌ لَكُمْ وَيُكَفِّرُ عَنكُم مِّن سَيِّئَاتِكُمْ وَاللهُ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ خَبِيرٌ الله . That they pay it to its rightful recipients between them and God. And he only said: 'It is issued as a fatwa that they repeat it secretly' as a precaution against the statement of some scholars that there is no repetition upon them because when they (the rebels) overpower the Muslims, their rule is like that of the imam by necessity; therefore, their appointment of judges and performance of Friday and Eid prayers and the like are valid. [1] His statement: 'to its rightful recipients' – with a kasra on the letter ha: meaning those who deserve zakat, who are the ones named as categories. [2] His statement: 'between them and God' – meaning no one knows it except him and his Lord, without the sultan or his deputies knowing, lest it be taken and usurped. [3] His statement: 'as a precaution... etc.' – the summary: there are three opinions in this issue: First: When they take zakat of apparent wealth, there is no repetition upon the owner whether he knows they spent it on the categories or not. Second: That the zakat is dropped by intending to give it to them as charity, so no need for repetition. These two opinions are weak, as the commentator will elaborate shortly. Third: What the author chose – that they repeat it secretly, and his apparent words indicate that it is obligatory upon them as a matter of conscience between him and God, and it is said that this ruling is precautionary. In any case, when the just imam prevails, they are not censured after the rebels took zakat of their apparent wealth because the imam protects them. Thus in al-Hidayah. (4) His statement: 'because when they overpower... etc.' – its summary: When the rebels overpower us and gain domination by force, their rule is like that of the just imam, and therefore whatever is valid from the just imam is valid from them – such as appointing judges in towns, undertaking the Eid and Friday prayers, and other rites of Islam: the outward acts that are made signs of it. So when they take zakat of our wealth, it is valid from them because they stand in the place of the imam, even if by force, so repetition is not obligatory on the owners. (1) al-Hidayah (2:199). The answer to this: That what is established by necessity is limited to its extent – meaning the appointment of judges and performance of Islamic rites is a necessity, unlike zakat, because the original principle in it is secret payment. Allah said: 'And if you conceal it and give it to the poor, that is better for you' (2:271). And regarding the statement of some scholars (2) [1] His statement: 'The answer to this' – meaning what some scholars mentioned, its explanation: It has been established in its place that what is established by necessity is restricted to the place of necessity and does not extend beyond it. The appointment of judges and performance of other Islamic rites are permitted for them out of necessity, because if it were not permitted, the organization of religious and worldly affairs would be corrupted. But there is no necessity to establish for them the authority to take zakat, because it is possible to pay it secretly. So if authority is not established for them, their taking it is without right. (2) His statement: 'Indeed the original principle in it is secret payment' – there is discussion from several aspects: First: It contradicts their explicit statements that the authority to take zakat on apparent wealth belongs to the sultan. If the original and best in paying zakat was concealment, it would not be so. Second: It contradicts their explicit statements that the best in obligatory charities, including zakat, is openness, and the virtue of concealment is only in voluntary charities, as in Khizanat al-Muftin and others. The open payment of zakat is better to remove suspicion. Third: The verse he used as proof that the original in zakat is concealment is taken as referring to voluntary charity, as stated in al-Kashshaf and others, so the argument is not complete. This is supported by the fact that the Prophet used to send collectors to the owners of wealth to take zakat, as is clear to anyone who studies hadith books. In summary, mentioning this principle is incorrect, and there is no need for it, for the purpose is achieved without it as we have indicated. (1) al-Baqarah (2:271), its full text: 'If you disclose your charitable expenditures, they are good; but if you conceal them and give them to the poor, it is better for you, and He will remove from you some of your misdeeds. And Allah is Acquainted with what you do.' (2) This statement is narrated from Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani; see al-Inayah (2:150), and al-Sarakhsi said in al-Mabsut (2:290) that it is the correct view.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether zakat that has been taken by rebel rulers (bughat) must be repeated secretly by the owner. The commentator explains that the author of the matn (likely al-Marghinani) chose the view that the owner must repeat the payment secretly, as a precaution against the opposing view that no repetition is needed. The opposing view argues that rebels, because they overpower Muslims, have the same legal standing as a legitimate imam by necessity, so their taking of zakat is valid and no repetition is required. The commentator then responds to this argument by invoking the principle that necessity is limited to its actual extent: while appointing judges and performing communal prayers are necessary to maintain order, the payment of zakat can be done secretly, so there is no necessity to grant the rebels authority to take it. He then critiques the claim that the original ruling for zakat is secrecy, pointing out three contradictions: (1) Hanafi scholars affirm that the ruler has authority over zakat on apparent wealth, which would not be the case if secrecy were the norm; (2) the best form of obligatory charity is openness, not concealment, as concealment is only recommended for voluntary charity; (3) the Quranic verse cited (2:271) is interpreted by major exegetes to refer to voluntary charity, not obligatory zakat. The commentator concludes that this argument is flawed and unnecessary, as the main point can be made without it. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, as stated by al-Sarakhsi, is that zakat taken by rebels must be repeated secretly.

Key Terms
بغاة (bughāt): Rebels who overpower a region and establish control, but whose rule is illegitimate in Islamic law.
ديانة (diyānatan): Religiously or according to one's conscience, in contrast to qadā'an (legally enforceable by a court).
ضرورة (ḍarūrah): Necessity that permits exceptional rulings but is limited to its actual scope.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary principle used by the Hanafi response to reject the validity of rebels taking zakat?
A) The rebels are sinners so their acts are invalid.
B) Necessity is limited to its extent; taking zakat is not essential for public order.
C) Zakat must be paid only to a legitimate imam.
D) The Quran forbids giving zakat to rebels.

Key Takeaway
When rebels take zakat by force, the owner must repeat the payment secretly because necessity does not grant them authority over wealth that can be paid discreetly.

Zakat: Publicity vs Concealment — Refuting the Claim of Secrecy
Refutation of concealment argument for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that obligatory zakat is best given publicly and refute the argument for concealment using the three points from the commentary.

Core Idea
Obligatory zakat is best announced publicly; the Quranic verse praising secrecy refers to voluntary charity.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: should zakat be given secretly or publicly? The passage refutes the claim that concealment is the original ruling, clarifying that obligatory zakat is better announced to ensure transparency and remove suspicion. We will analyze the three arguments presented by the commentator and understand the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed claim
Recognize that some Hanafi scholars (e.g., Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani) argued that the original ruling for zakat is concealment, citing Quran 2:271.
The claim is that zakat should be given secretly to avoid ostentation.
2
State the necessity limitation
Understand the commentator's initial response: the necessity that allows rulers to establish public rituals does not extend to zakat, because zakat can be performed secretly without corruption.
This sets the stage for refuting the need for rulers to collect zakat.
3
Analyze the three refutation points
Work through each point: (1) It contradicts the sultan's authority over apparent wealth; (2) It contradicts the preference for announcing obligatory charity; (3) The verse actually applies to voluntary charity, not zakat.
Each point undermines the claim that concealment is the original ruling.
4
Evaluate the evidence from practice
Note the prophetic practice: the Prophet sent collectors for zakat, indicating public collection. This prophetic sunnah supports the view that announcement is the norm.
The practice of the Prophet is a strong dalil for the Hanafi position.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
The commentator declares the concealment argument incorrect, and the relied-upon position is that obligatory zakat is best announced publicly, while secrecy is for voluntary charity.
This is the adopted fatwa in the Hanafi school.

The book of Zakat, Zakat of Wealth. And the answer to this: that what is established by necessity is limited to its scope, meaning the appointment of judges and the establishment of what is from the rituals of Islam is a necessity, unlike zakat, for the original ruling regarding it is performance in secret. There is no necessity to establish the authority of taking zakat for them, because it can be performed in secret. So when authority is not proven for them, their taking is without right.
(2) His saying: 'For the original ruling regarding it is performance in secret' has a discussion from several aspects:
First: It contradicts their explicit statements that the authority of taking zakat on apparent wealth belongs to the sultan, for if secrecy were the original and best in performing zakat, that would not be the case.
Second: It contradicts their explicit statements that the best in obligatory charities, including zakat, is to announce, and the virtue of secrecy is only in voluntary charities, as in 'Khizanat al-Muftiyin' and others. Public announcement of zakat is better to remove suspicion.
Third: The verse used as evidence that the original in zakat is concealment is applied to voluntary charities, as stated in 'al-Kashshaf' and others, so the analogy is not complete. It is supported by the fact that the Prophet used to send collectors to the owners of wealth to take zakat, as is not hidden from anyone who studies hadith books. In summary, mentioning this original ruling is incorrect and unnecessary, for the purpose is achieved without it as we have indicated.
(1) Al-Baqarah 2:271, its completion: 'If you disclose your charitable expenditures, they are good; but if you conceal them and give them to the poor, it is better for you, and He will remove from you some of your misdeeds. And Allah is Aware of what you do.'
(2) This saying is narrated from Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani; see: al-'Inayah (2:150), and al-Sarakhsi said in (al-Mabsut 2:290) it is the most correct.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hasiya) on the commentary of al-Wiqayah. It addresses an objection raised by some scholars that the original ruling for zakat is concealment, using the Quranic verse 2:271 as evidence. The commentator first clarifies the limitation of necessity: the appointment of judges and public rituals are necessities, but zakat can be performed secretly, so there is no need to grant rulers authority over its collection. Then, the commentator refutes the claim in three points: (1) It contradicts the established Hanafi position that the sultan has authority over collecting zakat on apparent wealth; if secrecy were best, this would not be so. (2) It contradicts the view that obligatory charity (including zakat) is best announced publicly to avoid suspicion, while secrecy is for voluntary charity. (3) The Quranic verse is actually about voluntary charity, not obligatory zakat. The practice of the Prophet sending collectors proves that zakat collection is public. Therefore, the argument is incorrect and unnecessary.

Key Terms
الزكاة (al-zakah): The obligatory charity on wealth, one of the five pillars of Islam.
الأصل فيها الأداء خفية (al-asl fiha al-ada' khufyah): The claim that the original ruling for zakat is to be performed secretly.
صدقات التطوع (sadaqat al-tatawwu'): Voluntary charity beyond the obligatory zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which type of charity is better given secretly?
A) Obligatory zakat
B) Voluntary charity (sadaqat al-tatawwu')
C) Both are better given secretly
D) Neither, all charity should be public

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that obligatory zakat is best announced publicly, while secrecy is recommended only for voluntary charity.

Paying Zakat to Tyrannical Rulers: Intention vs. Notification
Critical refinement on an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on paying zakat to a tyrannical ruler and explain why al-Maturidi's objection requiring notification is not accepted.

Core Idea
Zakat is discharged by paying a legally poor ruler, even without informing him, because intention in the heart suffices.

What happens if you pay zakat to an unjust ruler? According to the Hanafi school, the ruler is considered legally poor due to his unpaid debts and injustices. Thus, paying him with the intention of zakat fulfills the obligation, even if you do not tell him it is zakat. However, a prominent Hanafi scholar, Imam al-Maturidi, disagreed, insisting that the recipient must be informed. In this lesson, we examine the debate and the majority ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
The passage asks: Is zakat discharged when a person pays a tyrannical ruler with the intention of charity, without informing the ruler that the payment is zakat?
2
Understand the basis of legal poverty
The Hanafi position holds that the ruler is legally poor (faqir hukman) because he owes debts, usurpations, and other liabilities that exceed his wealth. This makes him a valid recipient of zakat.
Refer to the explanation of 'al-taba'at' in key terms.
3
Analyze al-Maturidi's objection
Al-Maturidi argued that informing the recipient is necessary because zakat is a pure act of worship requiring the recipient's awareness. Without it, the payer's intention is not fully realized.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The commentator refutes al-Maturidi, citing that intention in the heart alone suffices, supported by examples: paying a loan or gift while internally intending zakat. Informing is not a condition.
This is the preferred view (mufta bihi).

Qadi Khan mentioned in his Fatawa, and the author of al-Khulasa and others, from Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani: If the tyrannical ruler takes the charity of apparent wealth, the correct view is that the zakat falls from its owners, and they are not commanded to pay it again, because he has authority over taking, so his taking is valid, even if he does not place the charity in its proper place. And if he takes taxes or money by way of confiscation, and the owner of the money intends at the time of payment the zakat, some said it is not valid, and al-Sarakhsi said: The correct view is that the zakat falls from him. [2] His saying: because they; meaning because due to what is upon them of liabilities, they are poor, even if they are emirs in form. And 'liabilities' (at-taba'at) is the plural of taba'ah, which is what one is pursued for, and it refers to what is upon them of usurpations, incidents, debts, and wrongs such that their wealth is insufficient to pay them and be free from their responsibility, so they become poor legally, thus they are recipients of zakat, so paying zakat to them is valid. [3] His saying: Therefore he said... etc. The summary of the refutation: That in zakat it is necessary that the one being given charity be aware, and in the case of payment to rebels and tyrants, that is not possible, so how can zakat be performed by paying to them? And there is discussion, for requiring informing the recipient that it is zakat money has no evidence; rather, the intention of the payer in the heart suffices, even if his statement contradicts it. Hence they explicitly stated that if a man pays his money to a man who asked him for a loan and he calls it a loan, but intends zakat in his heart, it suffices if that man is a recipient. Similarly, if he calls it a gift and intends zakat, as stated in al-Qunyah and al-Bahr and others. (1) (al-Bahr al-Raiq 2:228); see also (al-Mabsut 12:94) etc.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement on a statement from the commentary. It discusses the ruling when a person pays zakat to tyrannical rulers with the intention of charity. The base text likely stated that if one pays unjust rulers intending charity to them, the zakat is discharged. The commentator explains that this is based on the rulers being considered poor due to their debts and injustices (legal poverty). Al-Maturidi refuted this, arguing that the recipient must be informed it is zakat, and that the payer lacked pure intention. The commentator then analyzes al-Maturidi's refutation, noting that informing is not a condition; the payer's internal intention suffices. Citing examples from Hanafi fiqh (e.g., calling a payment a loan or gift while intending zakat), the commentator upholds the validity of discharging zakat in such cases. The relied-upon position, according to al-Sarakhsi and others, is that the zakat falls from the payer.

Key Terms
السلطان الجائر (al-sultan al-ja'ir): A ruler who acts unjustly or oppressively.
التبعات (al-taba'at): Liabilities or obligations incurred through past actions, such as debts, usurpations, and injustices.
إعلام المتصدق عليه (i'lam al-mutasaddaq 'alayh): Informing the recipient that the payment is zakat.
تزييف (tazyif): Refutation or criticism of a view as weak.

Intention in Zakah and Payment to Unjust Rulers
Commentary on the necessity of pure intention in zakah and the ruling on paying to tyrant rulers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paying zakah to an unjust ruler and explain the role of intention in its validity.

Core Idea
Zakah requires pure intention; even coerced payment to a tyrant can discharge the obligation if the payer intends zakah.

This lesson examines a nuanced case in Hanafi fiqh: when a Muslim is forced to pay their zakah to an unjust ruler (sultan ja'ir). The central question is whether the obligation is fulfilled. The commentator draws from Al-Hidayah and clarifies that the payer's intention (niyyah) is the key factor, and that the ruler's own burdens may render him a de facto recipient, but only for the purpose of discharging the payer's liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? Paying zakah. What is the ruling? Two opinions: first (precautionary) does not suffice, second (qil) suffices with intention.
The first opinion is more precautionary (ahwat).
2
Locate the dalil
What is the proof for the second opinion? Analogy (qiyas) to prayer (coercion does not affect intention) and a narration from Al-Hidayah indicating removal of hardship.
The dalil is a combination of qiyas and athar.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the analogy work? Just as coercion in prayer does not invalidate intention, coercion in zakah payment does not; the narration shows that the oppressed payer's liability is dropped.
The operative principle is that coercion does not negate the validity of intention.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is intra-Hanafi disagreement: the majority view (first) vs. the permissive view (second). The first is more precautionary.
Both views are recorded in Hanafi sources.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The commentator leans towards the permissive view, but warns against misapplying it to allow rulers to take zakah for themselves.
The mufta bihi is the permissive view, as it removes hardship.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Book of Zakat - Zakat on Wealth. And also: It is not hidden that zakat is a pure act of worship like prayer, so it is not performed except with pure intention for Allah, and it does not exist. Then know that the expression mentioned in Al-Hidayah is: 'The recipients of zakat are the poor, and they do not pay it to them. And it is said: If he intends by payment to give charity to them, it falls from him. Similarly, payment to every unjust ruler, because they are poor due to the burdens incumbent upon them. And the first is more precautionary.' And whoever says that notification is necessary, his intention is that for the governor, so that the taker knows that he is a recipient and takes it or not, so he leaves it. For the zakah-giver often gives to a man thinking he is a recipient, but in reality he is rich or a Hashimi. [ ] He said: 'And also... etc.' This is another aspect to refute that statement. Its summary: Zakat is a pure independent act of worship like prayer and fasting, and not like acts that are means and mediums like ablution and the like. In such acts, pure intention for Allah is indispensable. Since it is not present in this situation, there is no validity. And there is also discussion: Firstly, because sharing an additional matter does not contradict pure intention, nor impair it being an act of worship, like the intention of trade in the journey of Hajj for Hajj. Secondly, because coercion to good deeds does not negate them being worship, as they have stated in its chapter. Similarly, the ruler taking by force does not negate it being worship, nor does it harm the existence of pure intention. The most that can be said is that when the intention is pure, without any sharing for other than worship, and proceeds from good choice and willingness of the soul, it is better and more hopeful for acceptance than an intention not like that. But that is another matter, for the discussion here is about the validity itself and the discharge of liability in the Hereafter and its absence.
[2] He said: 'Know... etc.' The purpose of quoting the expression from Al-Hidayah is to refute his contemporary Sheikh Nizam al-Din al-Harawi and invalidate his attribution to him of allowing the taking of zakat and tithes by rulers and their spending to their recipients based on them being poor, so they are recipients for it.
(1) This is the end from Al-Hidayah (1:103).
So you must reflect on this narration: does anything else come from it except the dropping of zakat from the oppressed, out of consideration for him and removal of hardship from him? And does this narration indicate that it is permissible for the Khawarij and people of injustice to take zakat and spend it on their needs, and not spend it to the poor, under the interpretation that they are poor? So look at this one who inserted another pillar into faith.
[2] And the complete expression of Al-Hidayah is: 'When the Khawarij take the kharaj and the sadaqah of grazing animals, they are not praised, because the Imam has not protected them, and collection is with protection. And they gave fatwa that they should repeat it without the kharaj, between themselves and Allah, because they are recipients of kharaj as they are fighters, and zakat's recipients are the poor, so they do not pay it to them. And it is said: If he intends by payment to give charity to them, it falls from him. Similarly, whatever is paid to every unjust, because they are poor due to the burdens upon them. And the first is more precautionary.' End.
(2) And raising of the obligation.
11] He said: 'That you reflect... etc.' Its summary: Nothing is understood from this expression except the dropping of zakat from the oppressed when he intends zakat at the time the oppressor takes it, because it contains removal of hardship and difficulty from him. And it is not understood in any way that it is permissible for the Khawarij, rebels, and oppressive sultans to take zakat money and not spend it to its recipients, but rather on themselves, relying on them being poor, so they themselves are recipients.
[2] He said: 'So look at this one who... etc.' He mentioned it with this title to demean or deter, like the saying of the people of Nimrod to our master Ibrahim, peace be upon him: 'Is this the one who mentions your gods?' The scholars of meanings have mentioned that this may be used to demean, and he emphasized it with a description that confirms that, which is breaking the consensus.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the requirement of pure intention (niyyah) in zakah and the ruling when zakah is paid to an unjust ruler (sultan ja'ir). The commentator opens by stating that zakah is a pure act of worship like salah, thus requiring sincere intention for Allah. He then cites from Al-Hidayah that the recipients of zakah are the poor, and there is a difference of opinion: the first opinion is that paying zakah to the ruler does not suffice because the ruler is not a valid recipient; the second opinion is that it suffices if the payer intends it as charity (sadaqah) because the ruler and his agents are considered poor due to the burdens they bear. The text notes that the first opinion is more precautionary (ahwat). The commentator then refutes the claim that notification (i'lam) to the ruler is necessary, clarifying that it is only for the ruler's knowledge. He further argues that even if the payer is coerced or the ruler takes it by force, it does not negate the validity of zakah, provided the payer has pure intention. However, the commentator warns against misinterpreting the narration to allow unjust rulers to take zakah for themselves, clarifying that the ruling only applies to the oppressed payer's liability being discharged, not to the ruler's action. The passage ends with a criticism of those who would insert another pillar into faith by allowing such misinterpretation.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention; the mental resolve to perform an act of worship solely for Allah.
مصرف (masrif): Recipient category of zakah; the eight categories specified in the Quran (e.g., poor).
سلطان جائر (sultan ja'ir): An unjust or tyrannical ruler who takes zakah by force without authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the purpose of notification (i'lam) to the ruler?
A) To make the ruler aware that the payer is discharging his obligation.
B) To allow the ruler to confirm the payer's intention.
C) To inform the ruler that the taker is a valid recipient.
D) To ensure the ruler does not take more than the due zakah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, paying zakah under coercion to an unjust ruler can still fulfill the obligation if the payer has pure intention, because the ruler's burdens make him a de facto recipient for the purpose of removing hardship from the oppressed.

No Zakat on the Property of a Taghlabi Child
Ruling on zakat for a Taghlabi child and distinction from 'ushr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for a Taghlabi child's wealth and distinguish it from the obligation of 'ushr on agricultural produce.

Core Idea
No zakat on a Taghlabi child's wealth, but 'ushr on land produce applies.

This passage from the kitab al-zakat clarifies a specific ruling regarding the Christian Arab tribe of Taghlib. While zakat is generally due on the property of Muslims who meet the conditions, the Hanafi school exempts the property of a Taghlabi child from zakat. However, the agricultural produce from lands subject to 'ushr (tithe) remains obligated. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying zakat and 'ushr rulings for non-Muslim subjects of the Islamic state.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the ruling
The subject is a child from the tribe of Taghlib (Christian Arab). The ruling: no zakat on his property (wealth).
The word 'الصبي التغلبي' refers specifically to a minor from the Christian Arab tribe of Banu Taghlib.
2
Note the distinction from 'ushr
The produce from his 'ushri land (land subject to the Islamic tithe) is excluded from this ruling; 'ushr is due.
The footnote clarifies that 'ففيه ضعف العشر' means the full 'ushr is due, just as on a Muslim child's land.
3
Compare with Muslim child
For a Muslim child, both zakat on wealth (if conditions met) and 'ushr on produce are due. For a Taghlabi child, only 'ushr applies.
This asymmetry arises from the special jizyah status of Banu Taghlib.
4
Understand the basis
The exemption is specific to the Taghlabi community due to their special jizyah arrangement. Other non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) do not have this exemption for zakat.
The passage implies that for other dhimmis, the ruling may differ – some schools require zakat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة زكاة الأموال
ولا شيء في مال الصبي التغلبي، وعلى المرأة ما على الرجل منهم. تَغْلِبُ : بكسر اللام ، أبو قبيلة ، والنسبة إليها تغلبية بفتح اللام استيحاشا" لتوالي الكسرتين، وربَّما قالوا بالكسر ، هكذا في «الصحاح». (٢) قوله : ولا شيء في مال الصبي التغلبي؛ أي في مال الزكاة، بخلاف الخارج في أرضه العشرية من الزروع والثَّمار ، ففيه ضعف العشر، كما يجب العشر في أرض الصبي المسلم. [٣] قوله : استيحاشاً؛ يعني كان القياس أن يقال في النسبة : تغلبي بكسر اللام، فاستوحشوا من توالى الكسرتين فقالوا : تغلبية بفتح اللام.
Chapter of Zakat: Zakat of Wealth. There is nothing (no zakat) in the property of the Taghlabi boy, and on the woman (of Taghlib) is the same as on the man from them. Taghlib: with kasrah on the lam, is a progenitor of a tribe, and the relative adjective (nisbah) to it is Taghlabiyyah with fat-ha on the lam due to aversion to consecutive two kasrahs, and sometimes they said with kasrah, thus in 'al-Sihah'. (2) His statement: 'There is nothing in the property of the Taghlabi boy,' i.e., in the property of zakat, unlike the produce from his 'ushri land (land subject to 'ushr) from crops and fruits, for it has two thirds of 'ushr (i.e., 'ushr is due), just as 'ushr is obligatory in the land of the Muslim boy. [3] His statement: 'istihashan' (aversion), it means the analogy was to say in the nisbah: Taghlabi with kasrah on the lam, but they felt aversion to the succession of two kasrahs, so they said Taghlabiyyah with fat-ha on the lam.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage states a ruling about zakat obligations for a child from the Christian tribe of Taghlib. The Hanafi position is that no zakat is due on the property of a Taghlabi child (i.e., a minor from the Christian Arab tribe of Taghlib). Similarly, a woman from this tribe has the same ruling as a man from them. The commentary clarifies that this refers to zakat on wealth (zakat al-mal), but it distinguishes zakat from 'ushr (the tithe on agricultural produce). If the Taghlabi child owns 'ushri land (land subject to the Islamic tithe), the produce from that land is subject to a reduced tithe: two-thirds of the regular 'ushr (i.e., 'ushr is due, but the text says 'two-thirds of 'ushr'? Actually, the text says 'fihi da'f al-'ushr' which is interpreted as 'one-tenth' by scholars; here it confirms that 'ushr is due on the produce as it is on the land of a Muslim child). The passage also includes a grammatical note explaining the correct nisbah (relative adjective) for Taghlib: although the qiyas would be 'Taghlabi' with a kasrah on the lam, due to aversion to consecutive kasrahs, they say 'Taghlabiyyah' with a fat-ha.

Key Terms
الصبي التغلبي (al-sabiyy al-taghlabiyy): A minor child from the Christian Arab tribe of Banu Taghlib, who pay jizyah with a special status.
العشور (al-'ushur): Tithe (one-tenth) on agricultural produce from 'ushri land.
النسبة إليها تغلبية بفتح اللام (al-nisbah ilayha Taghlabiyyah bi-fathi al-lam): The relative adjective (nisbah) for the tribe Taghlib is Taghlabiyyah with a fat-ha on the lam, due to aversion to consecutive kasrahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The full 'ushr (tenth) is due as on Muslim property.
C) Half of 'ushr is due.
D) It is subject to jizyah instead of 'ushr.

Key Takeaway
No zakat on the wealth of a Taghlabi child, but 'ushr on agricultural produce from 'ushri land remains obligatory.
